Innovation Lab","slug":"world-innovation-lab","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/449557974"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=449557974"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=449557974"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=449557974"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=449557974"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2316653,"date":"2022-05-17T06:00:06","date_gmt":"2022-05-17T13:00:06","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2316653"},"modified":"2022-05-17T11:43:05","modified_gmt":"2022-05-17T18:43:05","slug":"ai-powered-construction-management-platform-buildots-lands-60m","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/17\/ai-powered-construction-management-platform-buildots-lands-60m\/","title":{"rendered":"AI-powered construction management platform Buildots lands $60M"},"content":{"rendered":""ltr\">In the construction industry, managers can become disconnected from what’s happening on-site — particularly when dealing with pandemic-related disruptions. Among the top hurdles are staying on top of costs, communicating with all stakeholders and assessing risk related to aspects like contractor billing and performance. The disconnect can lead to delays and unanticipated expenses. One"http:\/\/www.ijimt.org\/vol8\/717-MP0022.pdf\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">study<\/a> found that 85% of construction projects over the course of a 70-year period experienced cost overruns and just 25% came close to their original deadlines.<\/p>\n"ltr\">The enormous addressable market — $1.3 trillion in the U.S.
"https:\/\/www.levelset.com\/blog\/us-construction-statistics-you-need-to-know\/#:~:text=In%202019%2C%20the%20US%20construction%20industry%20was%20worth%20%241.3%20trillion.&text=As%20of%202020%2C%20the%20construction,were%2011.2%20million%20construction%20employees.\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">alone<\/a> — continues to attract entrepreneurs like Roy Danon, who co-founded construction tech startup"https:\/\/buildots.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Buildots<\/a> in 2018 with Aviv Leibovici and Yakir Sudry. Graduates of the Israel Defense Forces (IDF), the founders created a platform that leverages AI and hardhat-mounted 360-degree cameras to capture images of ongoing construction projects during site inspections.<\/p>\n"ltr\">Buildots today announced that it raised $60 million in a Series C round co-led by Viola Growth and Eyal Ofer\u2019s O.G. Tech, with participation from TLV Partners, Lightspeed Venture Partners, Future Energy Ventures and Maor Investments. Danon says the new capital, which brings Buildots’ total raised to $106 million, will be put toward product development and expanding the Buildots team, particularly in Europe and North America.<\/p>\n"ltr\">“The construction industry has been going through major transformation over the past few years,” Danon told TechCrunch in an email interview. “Drivers of this change include rising demand for new commercial and residential projects, increasing complexity of these projects, and manpower shortage. Traditionally, contractors have suffered from low profit margins, but Buildots\u2019 solution is leading the charge to connect data to decision-making so that they can maximize revenue.”<\/p>\n"ltr\">The seed of the idea for Buildots came in 2017, 10 years after Danon, Leibovici and Sudry met in the IDF’s elite Talpiot unit. Without prior experience in or knowledge of the construction industry, the trio spent six months researching projects to better understand the challenges that construction companies and contractors face.<\/p>\n"speakable-summary\">"attachment_2317000\" style=\"width: 690px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">"caption-attachment-2317000\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-large wp-image-2317000\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/buildots.jpg?w=680\" alt=\"Buildots\" width=\"680\" height=\"383\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/buildots.jpg 1920w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/buildots.jpg?resize=150,84 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/buildots.jpg?resize=300,169 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/buildots.jpg?resize=768,432 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/buildots.jpg?resize=680,383 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/buildots.jpg?resize=1536,864 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/buildots.jpg?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" \/>"caption-attachment-2317000\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Image Credits:<\/strong> Buildots<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n"ltr\">Buildots analyzes project schedules, designs and other data to generate a model of an active construction site. When workers equip their hardhats with a compatible 360-degree camera and upload the footage to Buildots, the platform automatically compares features of the site — e.g. pipes under a kitchen sink — to the model to gauge progress, automatically blurring out people in the footage for compliance purposes.<\/p>"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n"ltr\">“Having operated in numerous and diverse regions, including North America, Europe, Asia-Pacific, and the Middle East, we have collected varied datasets that allow us to create extremely robust AI models,” Danon said. “For example, when a solution looks at hundreds of millions of sockets, it gets really good at recognizing issues and flagging mistakes. While most items look similar between construction sites, there\u2019s always that one client that decides to put a pink cubicle toilet that challenges our models at first glance.”<\/p>\n"ltr\">Buildots’ two-way integrations with planning platforms Oracle Primavera P6, Asta Powerproject and Microsoft Project are designed to allow instant timeline updates. Monthly progress reports, meanwhile, ostensibly help to validate subcontractor payment applications.<\/p>\n"ltr\">“Increasing visibility helps decision-makers reduce risk, improve cash flow, and save significant time,” Danon added. “[This gives] them the confidence to know their projects are being carried out as planned and in the most efficient way possible.”<\/p>\n"ltr\">Of course, Buildots isn’t the only company applying AI in the construction domain. Others include"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/30\/ai-powered-building-design-platform-beamup-emerges-from-stealth-with-15m\/\">BeamUp<\/a>, which is developing an AI-powered building design platform, and"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/12\/03\/ai-construction-startup-versatile-raises-a-20m-series-a\/\">Versatile<\/a>, which — like Buildots — captures and analyzes data across the construction site to provide a picture of construction progress.<\/p>\n"ltr\">Construction tech is a lucrative pursuit right now, thanks to the wider"https:\/\/www.globenewswire.com\/news-release\/2022\/02\/22\/2389055\/28124\/en\/United-States-Construction-Industry-is-Forecast-to-Grow-by-8-8-to-Reach-USD-1-355-097-million-in-2022-Despite-Near-Term-Challenges.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">industry boom<\/a>. In 2021, investment in construction startups reached a record $4.5 billion, triple the amount of money invested in 2020,"https:\/\/www.constructiontechnology.media\/news\/investment-in-construction-tech-hits-record-levels\/8016696.article\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">according<\/a> to Cemex Ventures.<\/p>\n"ltr\">When asked about traction and future plans, Danon said that Buildots’ revenue grew “tenfold” over the course of 2021 as the company’s customer base expanded to “dozens” of contractors.<\/p>\n"attachment_2317074\" style=\"width: 690px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">"caption-attachment-2317074\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-large wp-image-2317074\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Buildots_Side_by_side__2_.602e91a4cdac3.602e92e3755f0.602e992393bbe.jpg?w=680\" alt=\"Buildots\" width=\"680\" height=\"383\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Buildots_Side_by_side__2_.602e91a4cdac3.602e92e3755f0.602e992393bbe.jpg 1920w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Buildots_Side_by_side__2_.602e91a4cdac3.602e92e3755f0.602e992393bbe.jpg?resize=150,84 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Buildots_Side_by_side__2_.602e91a4cdac3.602e92e3755f0.602e992393bbe.jpg?resize=300,169 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Buildots_Side_by_side__2_.602e91a4cdac3.602e92e3755f0.602e992393bbe.jpg?resize=768,432 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Buildots_Side_by_side__2_.602e91a4cdac3.602e92e3755f0.602e992393bbe.jpg?resize=680,383 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Buildots_Side_by_side__2_.602e91a4cdac3.602e92e3755f0.602e992393bbe.jpg?resize=1536,864 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Buildots_Side_by_side__2_.602e91a4cdac3.602e92e3755f0.602e992393bbe.jpg?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" \/>"caption-attachment-2317074\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Image Credits:<\/strong> Buildots<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n"ltr\">“There are certainly companies trying to make construction more efficient. Examples include Avvir and Doxel in the U.S. and Disperse in the U.K. However, when it comes to syncing decision makers with data from building sites, Buildots does this with more depth and accuracy than anyone else,” Danon said. “Buildots has more than doubled the size of its team over the past year and recently surpassed the 200 mark. The new funding will be used to expand our R&D, sales, and marketing [organizations]. We expect to be 300 strong by the end of 2022.”<\/p>\n"ltr\">When contacted for comment, Viola Growth general partner Natalie Refuah said: “With top-notch technology and a superb team, Buildots offers immense potential in terms of efficiency and profitability. We are excited for their continued success capitalizing on this market.”<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"In the construction industry, managers can become disconnected from what’s happening on-site — particularly when dealing with pandemic-related disruptions. Growth","slug":"viola-growth","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576654451"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576654451"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576654451"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576654451"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576654451"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[{"id":576812993,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?taxonomy=_tc_cb_tag_taxonomy&term=o-g-tech-ventures-organization","name":"o-g-tech-ventures-organization","slug":"o-g-tech-ventures-organization","taxonomy":"_tc_cb_tag_taxonomy","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/crunchbase_tag\/576812993"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/crunchbase_tag"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/_tc_cb_tag_taxonomy"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?crunchbase_tag=576812993"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2319130,"date":"2022-05-17T05:30:26","date_gmt":"2022-05-17T12:30:26","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2319130"},"modified":"2022-05-17T11:57:55","modified_gmt":"2022-05-17T18:57:55","slug":"real-time-database-startup-imply-reaches-unicorn-status-with-100m-infusion","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/17\/real-time-database-startup-imply-reaches-unicorn-status-with-100m-infusion\/","title":{"rendered":"Real-time database startup Imply reaches unicorn status with $100M infusion"},"content":{"rendered":""speakable-summary\">The desire to extract value from enterprise data has only grown as the pandemic prompts organizations to digitize their operations. But organizations often lack the right set of tools to do so. According to a recent Fivetran"https:\/\/www.businesswire.com\/news\/home\/20220511005403\/en\/Over-80-Percent-of-Companies-Rely-on-Stale-Data-for-Decision-Making\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">survey<\/a>, 82% of companies are making decisions based on stale information, 85% of which say is leading to incorrect decisions and lost revenue.<\/p>\nWith the popularization of real-time database technologies, stale data and the problems surrounding it might soon become a thing of the past — if vendors’ sales pitches are to be believed. Real-time databases can deliver insights immediately, in theory, enabling companies to address line-of-business issues as they come up and act on short-term changes.<\/p>\nAs evidenced by the larger and larger funding tranches, investors believe that there’s a sizeable market for real-time databases. Last September,"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/09\/08\/real-time-database-platform-singlestore-raises-80m-more-now-at-a-940m-valuation\/\">SingleStore<\/a>, which provides a platform to help enterprises integrate, monitor and query their data as a single entity, raised $80 million in a financing round. Just today, another real-time database vendor,"http:\/\/imply.io\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Imply<\/a>, announced that it closed a $100 million Series D round that values the startup at a $1.1 billion post-money.<\/p>\nThoma Bravo led Imply’s round, with participation from OMERS Growth Equity, Bessemer Venture Funds, Andreessen Horowitz and Khosla Ventures. Co-founder and CEO Fangjin Yang says that the new money will be put toward product development and expanding the company’s workforce from 200 employees to 300 by the end of the year.<\/p>\n"attachment_2319290\" style=\"width: 3098px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">"caption-attachment-2319290\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-2319290 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/1568053570-fallback.jpg\" alt=\"Imply\" width=\"3088\" height=\"1790\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/1568053570-fallback.jpg 3088w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/1568053570-fallback.jpg?resize=150,87 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/1568053570-fallback.jpg?resize=300,174 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/1568053570-fallback.jpg?resize=768,445 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/1568053570-fallback.jpg?resize=680,394 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/1568053570-fallback.jpg?resize=1536,890 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/1568053570-fallback.jpg?resize=2048,1187 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/1568053570-fallback.jpg?resize=50,29 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 3088px) 100vw, 3088px\" \/>"caption-attachment-2319290\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Imply’s Apache Druid-powered query view.
Image Credits:<\/strong> Imply<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n“The industry at large is upon the next wave of technical hurdles for analytics based on how organizations want to derive value from data. The first wave in the 2000s was trying to solve the large-scale data processing and storage challenges, which [tools like] HDFS, MapReduce, and Spark addressed,” Yang told TechCrunch in an email interview. “The second wave in the 2010s was then trying to solve the problem of large-scale query processing, which created the emergence of cloud data warehouses (e.g., Snowflake, Redshift, and BigQuery) and distributed SQL engines (e.g., Impala, Presto, Athena). Now, the challenge organizations are trying to solve are large scale analytics applications enabling interactive data experiences. That\u2019s where … Imply comes in.”<\/p>\nBurlingame, California-based Imply was founded in 2015 by Yang, Gian Merlino and Vadim Ogievetsky. Yang was an R&D engineer at Cisco focusing on optimization algorithms for networking, while Merlino was a server software developer at Yahoo (full disclosure: TechCrunch’s parent company).<\/p>"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\nYang, Merlino and Ogievetsky met at Metamarkets, an analytics platform for programmatic advertising that was"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2017\/11\/03\/snap-metamarkets\/\">acquired<\/a> by Snap in 2017. While at Metamarkets, they developed Druid, an open source, distributed data store written in Java that uses a cluster of specialized processes to analyze high volumes of real-time and historical data.<\/p>\nDruid — which is currently used in production by companies including Netflix, Salesforce and Confluent — moved to an Apache license in 2015.<\/p>\n“What\u2019s consistent across companies using Druid … is their ability to unlock more value from data, specifically real-time, streaming events,” Yang said. “Where cloud data warehouses are for reports and dashboards described by infrequent queries by a handful of analysts, Druid enables analytics applications that power interactive, live conversations with data with a limitless number of internal stakeholders and external customers at instant query response times.”<\/p>\nImply builds fully managed databases using Druid. Moreover, Yang positions Imply as the “enterprise version” of Druid, providing ostensibly more capabilities and services than the standalone Druid project. For example, Imply recently launched Polaris, a cloud database service designed to simplify streaming, visualization, and other aspects of real-time analytics.<\/p>\n“From a business standpoint, the need for data-driven insights and applications has increased due changes brought about by the pandemic, which in turn has increased the need for Imply\u2019s technology,” Yang said. “[I]nsights are no longer confined to a predefined set of queries in a report. Organizations can now take real-time and historical events at tremendous scale (e.g., clickstream data, cloud application and services metrics, and internet of things telemetry) for operational intelligence, for real-time recommendations, and for extending insights to their customers.”<\/p>\n"embed breakout\">\n"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"GuS9MQFl2V\">"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/16\/start-up-solo-or-bring-on-a-co-founder-4-factors-to-consider\/\">Start up solo or bring on a co-founder? 4 factors to consider<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"“Start up solo or bring on a co-founder? 4 factors to consider” — TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/16\/start-up-solo-or-bring-on-a-co-founder-4-factors-to-consider\/embed\/#?secret=zCvYcmhESv#?secret=GuS9MQFl2V\" data-secret=\"GuS9MQFl2V\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\nImply stands to gain as enterprises increasingly favor the cloud for database management. Gartner once"https:\/\/mariadb.com\/survey\/cloud-global\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">predicted<\/a> that, by this year, 75% of all databases will be deployed or migrated to a cloud platform. Imply has competition in alternative databases and data warehouses like PostgreSQL, Snowflake, Elastic, and Clickhouse, but Yang asserts that the startup is sufficiently differentiated by its high concurrency and “value” — particularly in the areas of streaming and batch data.<\/p>\nBarring thorough comparisons of each platform, we’ll have to take Yang’s word for it. But for what it’s worth, Imply claims to have over 150 customers, including Atlassian, Cisco ThousandEyes, InterContinental Exchange and Reddit.<\/p>\n“Applications built on Imply\u2019s database are accessed by many thousands of users,” said Yang, who demurred when asked about Imply’s current revenue. “Druid is unlocking a whole new world of analytics use cases, and it\u2019s creating tremendous value for organizations as they undergo digital transformations.”<\/p>\nTo date, Imply has raised $215 million in venture capital.<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"The desire to extract value from enterprise data has only grown as the pandemic prompts organizations to digitize their operations. But organizations often lack the right set of tools to do so. According to a recent Fivetran survey, 82% of companies are making decisions based on stale information, 85% of which say is leading to tags\/577017371"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=577017371"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=577017371"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=577017371"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=577017371"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":1044469,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/khosla-ventures\/","name":"Khosla Ventures","slug":"khosla-ventures","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/1044469"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=1044469"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=1044469"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=1044469"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=1044469"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":576793974,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/omers-growth-equity\/","name":"OMERS Growth Equity","slug":"omers-growth-equity","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576793974"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576793974"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576793974"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576793974"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576793974"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":75547,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/real-time\/","name":"real-time","slug":"real-time","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/75547"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=75547"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=75547"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=75547"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=75547"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2318554,"date":"2022-05-17T05:00:12","date_gmt":"2022-05-17T12:00:12","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2318554"},"modified":"2022-05-17T12:40:04","modified_gmt":"2022-05-17T19:40:04","slug":"a-team-emerges-from-stealth-with-a-gig-marketplace-for-product-specialists","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/17\/a-team-emerges-from-stealth-with-a-gig-marketplace-for-product-specialists\/","title":{"rendered":"A.Team emerges from stealth with a gig marketplace for product specialists"},"content":{"rendered":""ltr\">The gig economy has, to use a well-worn word, disrupted industries from ride-hailing to quick-service restaurants. Contract work has its"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2018\/08\/08\/study-flags-poor-quality-working-conditions-for-remote-gig-workers\/\">downsides<\/a>, namely on the pay and benefits side of the equation. But sheer force of will and"https:\/\/qz.com\/1556194\/the-gig-economy-is-quietly-undermining-a-century-of-worker-protections\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">unit economics beneficial to corporations<\/a>\u00a0have catapulted it into the mainstream.<\/p>\n"ltr\">A 2019"https:\/\/newsroom.mastercard.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/05\/Gig-Economy-White-Paper-May-2019.pdf\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">study<\/a> by Mastercard estimated that the global gig economy now generates $204 billion in gross volume. It expects that volume to grow 17% by 2023.<\/p>\n"ltr\">A number of entrepreneurs push back against the notion that the gig economy is a net negative, pointing to the flexibility it provides to both workers and employers. Raphael Ouzan and Kobi Matsri are among this cohort, having founded"https:\/\/www.a.team\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">A.Team<\/a>, a gig marketplace for product engineers, in early 2020.<\/p>\n"ltr\">“We saw that highly-skilled tech workers wanted to escape the rigid structures of full-time work, but the [traditional] gig economy wasn\u2019t an answer for them, since it was so commoditizing and capped with simple, task-based work,” Ouzan told TechCrunch in an email interview. “Then came the obvious insight: Solving problems that matter requires a team of diverse skill sets, background, and perspectives. Team is the core unit of work of the knowledge economy, and yet had never been productized in the world of online work.”<\/p>\n"speakable-summary\">"attachment_2318672\" style=\"width: 2230px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">"caption-attachment-2318672\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-2318672 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/60aee46d35df4af311836785_team-management-main-image.png\" alt=\"A.Team\" width=\"2220\" height=\"1628\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/60aee46d35df4af311836785_team-management-main-image.png 2220w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/60aee46d35df4af311836785_team-management-main-image.png?resize=150,110 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/60aee46d35df4af311836785_team-management-main-image.png?resize=300,220 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/60aee46d35df4af311836785_team-management-main-image.png?resize=768,563 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/60aee46d35df4af311836785_team-management-main-image.png?resize=680,499 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/60aee46d35df4af311836785_team-management-main-image.png?resize=1536,1126 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/60aee46d35df4af311836785_team-management-main-image.png?resize=2048,1502 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/60aee46d35df4af311836785_team-management-main-image.png?resize=50,37 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 2220px) 100vw, 2220px\" \/>"caption-attachment-2318672\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Building product teams with A.Team.
Image Credits:<\/strong> A.Team<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n"ltr\">Ouzan claims that A.Team, which today emerged from stealth with $60 million in funding, differs from traditional gig platforms in that it “bring[s] world-class product builders together as cloud-based teams and connect[s] them with companies that had meaningful product missions.” That’s a lot of jargon and positive framing, but the crux is that A.Team helps companies assemble teams of vetted specialists to design and\/or bring products to market.<\/p>\n"ltr\">A.Team launched at the start of the pandemic, when crippling layoffs were hitting the tech industry. Ouzan says that thousands of engineers, designers and product managers signed up to build products, including mask distribution, contact tracing and vaccine manufacturing software.<\/p>"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n"ltr\">The normalization of remote work fueled growth, too, as product specialists were increasingly able to work from home. “We\u2019d never publicly launched A.Team as a company, but grew to a [referral- and] members-only network of over 250 clients and 4,000 builders while still in stealth and invite-only over the past two years — all through word-of-mouth,” Ouzan said. “We started enabling product builders to team up with their peers to work on problems that matter to them while enjoying full autonomy and income.”<\/p>\n"ltr\">Fascinatingly, A.Team leveraged its own network in combination with a full-time staff to build and expand the A.Team platform. A.Team’s contractors and full-timers created what Ouzan called the TeamGraph, which takes into account a gig candidate’s work experience and “behavioral analytics” to piece together product teams for companies. The TeamGraph is a semantic graph that attempts to establish the relationships between industry experience, skills, roles and expertise, pulling data from a range of sources and using machine learning to optimize the graph with inputs from A.Team’s Team Pulse feature. Team Pulse enables customers to rate the A.Team members they\u2019re working with and members to rate each other — honestly and not maliciously, one would hope.<\/p>\n"ltr\">“Our algorithm can … learn what [A. Team users are] interested in based on behavioral data, not just self-reported data. Think of it like a smart inbox for teams and missions,” Ouzan said. “With TeamGraph, we don\u2019t recommend people for roles \u2014 we recommend teams for missions. We mitigate bias in our recommendations by ensuring the algorithm is blind to any demographic or location data.”<\/p>\n"ltr\">Like any other jobs platform, A.Team also provides recommendations to gig searchers and teams, leaning on connections, complementary skill sets, and projects to identify top matches.<\/p>\n"ltr\">“A.Team is popularizing the concept of elastic resourcing by way of cloud-based teams, which will make companies and builders more resilient to potential market downswings. It\u2019s a smarter way to scale for growth,” Ouzan argues. “The power dynamics have changed, and the best and a lot of the top tech talent in the world want the freedom and flexibility to work on what matters to them, not the rigid structures of a full-time job.”<\/p>\n"attachment_2318671\" style=\"width: 1544px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">"caption-attachment-2318671\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-2318671 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/624520dcacdce298564a5bae_how-it-works-2.png\" alt=\"A.Team\" width=\"1534\" height=\"940\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/624520dcacdce298564a5bae_how-it-works-2.png 1534w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/624520dcacdce298564a5bae_how-it-works-2.png?resize=150,92 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/624520dcacdce298564a5bae_how-it-works-2.png?resize=300,184 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/624520dcacdce298564a5bae_how-it-works-2.png?resize=768,471 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/624520dcacdce298564a5bae_how-it-works-2.png?resize=680,417 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/624520dcacdce298564a5bae_how-it-works-2.png?resize=50,31 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1534px) 100vw, 1534px\" \/>"caption-attachment-2318671\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Image Credits:<\/strong> A.Team<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n"ltr\">The evidence is mixed on this. While it’s true that many"https:\/\/www.wsj.com\/articles\/people-quit-full-time-jobs-for-contract-gigs-and-make-six-figures-great-resignation-11647291183\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">professionals<\/a> quit full-time jobs for contract work during the pandemic, particularly in project management and consulting,"http:\/\/b2b-assets.glassdoor.com\/benefits-employees-want-most-2017.pdf\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">surveys<\/a> show that the benefits and perks that come along with salaried work remain highly desirable. As for whether a greater reliance on contract workers can insulate companies against economic headwinds, that’s proven to be untrue in certain industries, like health care, which during the pandemic paid contractors"https:\/\/www.healthcarefinancenews.com\/news\/hospitals-paying-24-billion-more-labor-during-covid-19-pandemic\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">significantly more<\/a> than full-time workers to address staffing shortfalls.<\/p>\n"ltr\">Ouzan asserts that the tech industry is somewhat unique in its orientation around product lifecycles, which call for niche expertise. In addition to bringing products from ideation to production, companies can use A.Team to inject missing skills into product teams, he says, or deliver supplementary teams to work on additional lines of business.<\/p>\n"ltr\">There’s interest in A.Team, clearly, with 25 new company clients joining the platform per month. Revenue grew 7.4x in 2021 and gross merchandise value (e.g. total revenue from sales) recently crossed $42 million, according to Ouzan, thanks to a customer base that includes McGraw Hill and The Economist. But as A.Team prepares to onboard 100 new companies per month, it remains to be seen whether the flexibility — and pay, for that matter — will continue to attract workers to the platform. It’s often a delicate balancing act with gig marketplaces. For example, early on in the pandemic, a"https:\/\/time.com\/5836868\/gig-economy-coronavirus\/\">flood<\/a> of newly jobless employees cut deeply into gig worker incomes.<\/p>\n"ltr\">“Through modular, cloud-based teams, we\u2019re empowering companies to elastically scale up and down their product resources based on the mission at hand and stage of product development,” Ouzan said. “A.Team is an entirely new way of working for the top product builders that have left FAANG companies and want the freedom to work on meaningful product missions with teammates they love. They work in teams on missions that last 12 to 19 months on average, and make $130 per hour on average. Making $100,000 a year on Fiverr is the outlier; at A.Team, it’s the starting point.”<\/p>\n"ltr\">A.Team’s funding came from a $55 million Series A round co-led by Tiger Global Management, Insight Partners and Spruce Capital Partners, and a previously undisclosed $5 million seed round. The seed round was led by NFX, joined by Box Group, Village Global and firstminute Capital, with participation from (unsurprisingly) a former Upwork CEO and co-founder of Fiverr.<\/p>\n"ltr\">Ouzan says that the capital will be put toward expanding the core A.Team platform and creating an ecosystem of independent product builders, companies, partners and investors. The company currently employs 75 people between staffers and contractors and expects to grow that number to 170 by 2022.<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"The gig economy has, to use a well-worn word, disrupted industries from ride-hailing to quick-service restaurants. design","slug":"product-design","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/13948"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=13948"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=13948"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=13948"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=13948"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":4621,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/startup\/","name":"startup","slug":"startup","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/4621"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=4621"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=4621"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=4621"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=4621"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2311970,"date":"2022-05-17T04:30:43","date_gmt":"2022-05-17T11:30:43","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2311970"},"modified":"2022-05-17T14:26:14","modified_gmt":"2022-05-17T21:26:14","slug":"2311970","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/17\/2311970\/","title":{"rendered":"Fashinza, a B2B supply chain marketplace for fashion brands, raises $100M"},"content":{"rendered":""speakable-summary\">The pandemic has majorly affected the global supply chain, with 60% of U.S. adults in an August 2021 Gallup"https:\/\/news.gallup.com\/poll\/353312\/consumers-felt-supply-chain-problems.aspx\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">survey<\/a> saying that they’ve been unable to get a product they wanted in the past two months because of shortages. Bearing the brunt of the impact is the fashion industry, which employs millions of workers at retail stores, suppliers and manufacturing factories around the world. Bangladesh, one of the largest exporters of ready-made garments, saw export earnings plunge from $34.13 billion in 2018 to less than $28 billion in 2020 as Western brands wrestled with pandemic-related border restrictions.<\/p>\n"http:\/\/Fashinza.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Fashinza<\/a>, a Gurgaon, India-based supply chain “marketplace” for fashion brands and retailers, was co-founded months before the disruptions. But CEO Pawan Gupta says that the platform was designed to handle exactly these types of supply chain challenges by providing"font-weight: 400;\"> access to fulfillment options that wouldn’t normally be available to international companies.<\/span><\/p>\n"font-weight: 400;\">“While exploring [the] business-to-consumer fashion ecommerce [industry], we were shocked by the serpentine supply chains,” Gupta, who co-launched Fashinza with <\/span>"font-weight: 400;\">Abhishek Sharma and Jamil Ahmad, told TechCrunch via email. <\/span>"font-weight: 400;\">“Even though brands were marking up their retail price at 75% to 80% margins, they were still making only around 8% to 10% profits and losing money due to high inventory wastage or going out of stock. [They] struggled with … opacity due to multiple middlemen and their manufacturers being thousands of miles away.”<\/span><\/p>\n"font-weight: 400;\">Gupta describes Fashinza’s product as “design to delivery” in the sense that it lets brands not only find manufacturers and place bulk orders, but analyze trending designs in fashion. Customers can also use Fashinza to track time and action calendars, a tool used in the apparel industry to follow up on manufacturing milestones to ensure timely delivery.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n"attachment_2312197\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">"caption-attachment-2312197\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2312197\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/techpack.png\" alt=\"Fashinza\" width=\"1024\" height=\"1235\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/techpack.png 2720w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/techpack.png?resize=124,150 124w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/techpack.png?resize=249,300 249w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/techpack.png?resize=768,926 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/techpack.png?resize=564,680 564w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/techpack.png?resize=1274,1536 1274w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/techpack.png?resize=1698,2048 1698w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/techpack.png?resize=41,50 41w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/>"caption-attachment-2312197\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Fashinza’s B2B supply chain marketplace.
Image Credits:<\/strong> Fashinza<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n"font-weight: 400;\">On the production side, Fashinza partners with factories to run its software stack, dubbed FactoryOS, for tasks in sampling, inventory and finance. The software tracks the lifecycles of garments and uses the data to train algorithms for matching brands with suppliers, Gupta said, and predicting metrics like turnaround time.<\/span><\/p>\nIn an endorsement of"font-weight: 400;\">Fashinza’s approach to supply chain management<\/span>, the company today announced that it raised $100 million in Series B funding ($60 million in equity and $40 million in debt) co-led by"font-weight: 400;\">Prosus Ventures and Westbridge, with participation from Accel, Elevation and ADQ at a $300 billion valuation. The round brings Fashinza’s total raised to $135 million, which Gupta says is being used to refine the company’s supply chain technology and expand into new markets, including raw materials procurement.<\/span><\/p>"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n“"font-weight: 400;\">Business-to-business marketplaces are here to stay. We can\u2019t imagine a world where, even in 2030, brands would need to make 100 calls, send 200 emails, and wait for six months for [a] bulk order,” Gupta said. “The entire experience is broken and doesn\u2019t work in this fast-paced world. But the solutions … need to be vertical and very customized to … industries.”<\/span><\/p>\nAn expanding market<\/h2>\n"font-weight: 400;\">Prior to starting Fashinza, Gupta co-founded Curofy, a social networking app for doctors, while <\/span>"font-weight: 400;\">Sharma previously helped to found e-commerce retailer OfferBean. Together with Ahmad, they launched Fashinza in 2020, which now employs a workforce of 200 people. Gupta expects headcount to expand to 250 by the end of the year.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n"font-weight: 400;\">Fashinza makes money by charging suppliers a “usage-based” fee on every order and by providing value-added services like logistics, fintech and business-to-business payments to both brands and manufacturers. Gupta asserts that Fashinza is able to achieve cost savings by <\/span>"font-weight: 400;\">improving the unit economics on the supply side, leveraging “unutilized capacity” and “improving production efficiency” through tech and data.<\/span><\/p>\nCertainly,"font-weight: 400;\">Fashinza has no shortage of competition in a supply chain management market that Statista"https:\/\/www.statista.com\/statistics\/1181996\/supply-chain-management-market-size-worldwide\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">predicts<\/a> could be worth $30.91 billion by 2026, up from $19.58 billion in 2022.
"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/04\/14\/shipium-e-commerce-retailers-supply-chain-tech-amazon\/\">Shipium<\/a> gives e-commerce retailers Amazon-like supply chain tech, while"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/06\/09\/shelflife-a-marketplace-for-raw-materials-raises-3-million-seed-round\/\">ShelfLife<\/a> offers a marketplace of raw material suppliers based on what brands actually need. There’s also sustainable sourcing platforms like"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/09\/14\/index-leads-12-2m-seed-in-sourceful-a-data-play-to-make-supply-chains-greener\/\">Sourceful<\/a>, which slot somewhere alongside supply chain finance platforms including"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/12\/09\/sfs-tradeshift-a-supply-chain-finance-platform-raises-200m\/\">Tradeshift<\/a>.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\nGupta argues that"font-weight: 400;\">Fashinza’s focus on the fashion industry sufficiently differentiates it, pointing to the customer uptake so far. He claims that over 200 brands and 150 factories are currently using the platform, concentrated mostly in India, Bangladesh, China, the U.S., the U.K., the United Arab Emirates and Vietnam.<\/span><\/p>\n"embed breakout\">\n"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"UCUUa8diNp\">"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/08\/31\/6-tips-for-establishing-your-startups-global-supply-chain\/\">6 tips for establishing your startup’s global supply chain<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"“6 tips for establishing your startup’s global supply chain” — TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/08\/31\/6-tips-for-establishing-your-startups-global-supply-chain\/embed\/#?secret=yA0Fz8YnDs#?secret=UCUUa8diNp\" data-secret=\"UCUUa8diNp\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\nHistorically, the challenge has been convincing fashion and apparel brands to adopt technologies to modernize legacy processes, including sourcing. For example, a 2020 McKinsey"https:\/\/www.mckinsey.com\/~\/media\/mckinsey\/industries\/retail\/our%20insights\/time%20for%20change%20how%20to%20use%20the%20crisis%20to%20make%20fashion%20sourcing%20more%20agile%20and%20sustainable\/time-for-change-how-to-use-the-crisis-to-make-fashion-sourcing-more-agile-and-sustainable.pdf\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">study<\/a> found that while 74% of brands anticipate the digitization of product development and sourcing will accelerate, only 20% plan to make technology for country and supplier selection a common practice.<\/p>\nBut Gupta believes that"font-weight: 400;\">Fashinza has the stuff — and the financing — to succeed. Indeed, the startup stands to benefit from the continued investment boom in the supply chain management market, which saw an <\/span>"font-weight: 400;\">$11.3 billion injection from venture firms last year.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n"font-weight: 400;\">“The solution brought about by Fashinza is essentially tech-driven, which sets us apart from our competitors. Imagine the disruptions brought about by Uber and Amazon in their respective industries. Fashinza is doing something similar in the business-to-business apparel manufacturing sector,” Gupta said. “<\/span>"font-weight: 400;\">End-to-end production can be managed through Fashinza\u2019s platform with … transparency and control — with no need for sourcing managers to leave their offices, no need to depend on multiple middlemen, and no scope for unannounced delays.”<\/span><\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"The pandemic has majorly affected the global supply chain, with 60% of U.S. adults in an August 2021 Gallup survey saying that they’ve been unable to get a product they wanted in the past two months because of shortages. Ventures","slug":"prosus-ventures","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576710036"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576710036"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576710036"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576710036"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576710036"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":4621,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/startup\/","name":"startup","slug":"startup","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/4621"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=4621"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=4621"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=4621"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=4621"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2318986,"date":"2022-05-16T09:09:13","date_gmt":"2022-05-16T16:09:13","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2318986"},"modified":"2022-05-16T10:25:05","modified_gmt":"2022-05-16T17:25:05","slug":"keelvar-raises-24m-to-automate-procurement-in-the-supply-chain","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/16\/keelvar-raises-24m-to-automate-procurement-in-the-supply-chain\/","title":{"rendered":"Keelvar raises $24M to automate procurement in the supply chain"},"content":{"rendered":""speakable-summary\">Supply chain disruptions caused — or exacerbated — by the pandemic continue to affect businesses in a range of industries. For example, 36% of small businesses responding to a U.S. Census Small Business Pulse last year"https:\/\/www.whitehouse.gov\/cea\/written-materials\/2021\/06\/17\/why-the-pandemic-has-disrupted-supply-chains\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">reported<\/a> delays with domestic suppliers. Each missed shipment or material shortage can be costly. In a 2021 Deloitte"https:\/\/www2.deloitte.com\/us\/en\/pages\/about-deloitte\/articles\/press-releases\/supply-chain-disruptions-increased-costs-for-nearly-half-of-cfos-surveyed-in-the-third-quarter-deloitte-cfo-signals-survey.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">survey<\/a>, more than 40% of chief financial officers indicated that supply chain shortages or delays increased their companies\u2019 expenditures by 5% or more.<\/p>\nSupply chain technology companies have risen to prominence during the shortages, promising a solution to a problem that looks unlikely to abate anytime soon. One of these vendors is"https:\/\/www.keelvar.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Keelvar<\/a>, a Cork, Ireland-based supply chain analytics platform that weighs different sourcing scenarios to guide customers to decisions for their supply chains.<\/p>\nKeelvar is headed by Alan Holland, who left his position as a lecturer in AI at the University of College Cork to found the startup in 2012.<\/p>\n“My goal was to use my specialist knowledge in optimization, game theory, and mechanism design to commercialize advances in AI for procurement teams,” Holland told TechCrunch in an email interview. “[O]ur solutions have helped our customers adapt to ever more volatile conditions, notably in the transportation market, where our [platform has] allowed customers to source efficiently in an adverse environment.”<\/p>\nOrganizations that rely on the supply chain, which is practically all of them, engage in a process called procurement. Procurement entails acquiring goods and services from suppliers who typically compete for business by submitting bids that companies evaluate. Suppliers with the most attractive bid are awarded a contract, the terms of which are subject to negotiation.<\/p>\n"attachment_2319121\" style=\"width: 2542px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">"caption-attachment-2319121\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-2319121 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/61a9f661e073617445e35202_Website-header-2x-v2.png\" alt=\"Keelvar\" width=\"2532\" height=\"1754\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/61a9f661e073617445e35202_Website-header-2x-v2.png 2532w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/61a9f661e073617445e35202_Website-header-2x-v2.png?resize=150,104 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/61a9f661e073617445e35202_Website-header-2x-v2.png?resize=300,208 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/61a9f661e073617445e35202_Website-header-2x-v2.png?resize=768,532 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/61a9f661e073617445e35202_Website-header-2x-v2.png?resize=680,471 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/61a9f661e073617445e35202_Website-header-2x-v2.png?resize=1536,1064 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/61a9f661e073617445e35202_Website-header-2x-v2.png?resize=2048,1419 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/61a9f661e073617445e35202_Website-header-2x-v2.png?resize=50,35 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 2532px) 100vw, 2532px\" \/>"caption-attachment-2319121\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Evaluating procurement bids with Keelvar.
Image Credits:<\/strong> Keelvar<\/p><\/div><\/p>\nKeelvar allows customers to canvass an array of direct and indirect procurement bid information from suppliers and then analyze multiple awarding scenarios based on those criteria and other constraints. (Direct procurement is spending on goods and services that drive tangible profit, whereas indirect procurement is spending on goods and services needed for day-to-day operations.) Using the platform, they can also launch and run new bidding events. Algorithms sort through data on supply chain disruptions and vendors, cleansing it and extracting information before offering recommendations.<\/p>"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\nDuring the pandemic, Holland said that pharmaceutical companies used Keelvar to spot bad actors and inflated prices in the supply chain, and responded by rerouting goods through other means of transportation (e.g., via ground instead of air).<\/p>\n“AI-powered sourcing bots are essentially agents designed to execute several tasks and reason about inputs they receive, such as identifying suppliers to invite to a bidding event, managing supplier communications and bid analysis, and recommending award decisions,” Keelvar explains on its website. “[The]"font-size: 1rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">bots can establish spot bidding or mini-tender events within a matter of minutes, managing and automating mundane tasks such as inviting carriers, collecting and validating bid data, messaging bid status updates, conducting necessary rate card and lane information lookups, and generating award recommendations.”<\/span><\/p>\nVenture capitalists see the opportunity in the supply chain. Last year was a banner year, when VCs put $11.3 billion in financing toward vendors in the sector,"https:\/\/news.crunchbase.com\/news\/supply-chain-vc-startup-funding\/\">according<\/a> to Crunchbase. Keelvar is a beneficiary, having today closed a $24 million Series B funding round led by 83North with participation from Elephant, Mosaic, and Paua.<\/p>\n“Enterprises were blindsided when the pandemic shut down the global supply chain. As issues persist and show no sign of relenting, C-suites are finally recognizing that intelligent automation is a must-have,” 83North partner Philip Chopin said in a statement. “Keelvar\u2019s unique automation and optimization solutions empower procurement teams by helping them easily define their needs and react faster to market changes. The company\u2019s blue-chip customer list and incredible retention and satisfaction rates are a powerful testament to their technology, team, and vision.”<\/p>\nKeelvar competes with a number of companies in the procurement solutions space, including Fairmarkit, Tealbook, and"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/28\/contingent-fundraise\/\">Contingent<\/a>. But while remaining vague about Keelvar’s technological advantages, as well as revenue, Holland pointed to the company’s overall growth in recent months. Keelvar, which plans to expand its 85-person headcount to over 130 by the end of the year, currently has over 70 enterprise customers and “thousands” of paying users.<\/p>\n“[Recently,] we\u2019ve significantly expanded our customer base and team, as well as successfully launched [air] and ocean bots for sourcing automations,” Holland said. “We\u2019ve [also] successfully grown as a remote-first organization, doubling our workforce.”<\/p>\nThe Series B brings Keelvar’s total raised to $43 million. Holland said that the company plans to put it toward product development and expanding in the U.S.<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"Keelvar closed a $24 million Series B funding round led by 83North with participation from Elephant, Mosaic, and chain","slug":"supply-chain","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/17010"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=17010"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=17010"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=17010"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=17010"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2317862,"date":"2022-05-16T07:00:51","date_gmt":"2022-05-16T14:00:51","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2317862"},"modified":"2022-05-16T10:48:53","modified_gmt":"2022-05-16T17:48:53","slug":"marketing-data-management-platform-claravine-nabs-16m","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/16\/marketing-data-management-platform-claravine-nabs-16m\/","title":{"rendered":"Marketing data management platform Claravine nabs $16M"},"content":{"rendered":""speakable-summary\">"http:\/\/claravine.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Claravine<\/a>, a self-described marketing data platform, today announced that it raised $16 million in a Series B round led by Five Elms Capital with participation from"font-weight: 400;\">Grayhawk Capital, Next Frontier Capital, Peninsula Ventures, Kickstart Fund and Silverton Partners<\/span>. CEO Verl Allen says that the new money, which brings the company’s total raised to $27.9 million, will be used to double Claravine’s headcount to 88 employees by the end of the year and support product R&D.<\/p>\n"font-weight: 400;\">Claravine was founded in 2012 as Tracking First, a company focused on streamlining the tracking code process for large organizations. Tracking code is a snippet of code that tracks the activity of a website visitor by collecting data and sending it to an analytics module, usually for marketing purposes.<\/span><\/p>\nAccording to Allen, Tracking First had “gritty founders” who “knew the space well” and had “high-quality” customers, but the focus was too narrow. “T"font-weight: 400;\">here was a realization that there was a bigger underlying problem that was being ignored in the market, which our solution had the potential to address,” Allen told TechCrunch in an email interview. “In 2018, I joined as CEO and helped the organization — now Claravine — to grow and expand the ways we could help the largest organizations in the world take a proactive approach to their data.”<\/span><\/p>\nClaravine’s product is designed to"font-weight: 400;\"> help enterprises control what flows through their tech stack, especially business intelligence and analytics software, and manage their marketing data standards — the blueprints for defining common formats for data across regions, teams and campaigns<\/span>"font-weight: 400;\">. Via an API and integrations with platforms including Adobe Experience Manager and Workfront as well as media platforms like Google Ads, Claravine supports <\/span>"font-weight: 400;\">teams in managing parameters of these standards over time.<\/span><\/p>\n"font-weight: 400;\">“[F]or many organizations, decision-makers have to rely on untrustworthy data for business decisions … [These] d<\/span>"font-weight: 400;\">ecision-makers rely not just on technologies and data but humans, and that creates a large possibility for error in the data entry process, exacerbated by all the disconnected technologies and teams,” Allen said. “This <\/span>"font-weight: 400;\">is why our solution is built to engrain standards into the way business teams work and collaborate as they create and modify data. By facilitating a common understanding of standards as inputs are generated and reviewed, organizations have greater control early on, whatever their needs. And downstream data users can move with more confidence and speed when using this data to make decisions.”<\/span><\/p>\n"attachment_2318000\" style=\"width: 3210px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">"caption-attachment-2318000\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-2318000 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/User-adobe.png\" alt=\"Claravine\" width=\"3200\" height=\"2146\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/User-adobe.png 3200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/User-adobe.png?resize=150,101 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/User-adobe.png?resize=300,201 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/User-adobe.png?resize=768,515 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/User-adobe.png?resize=680,456 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/User-adobe.png?resize=1536,1030 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/User-adobe.png?resize=2048,1373 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/User-adobe.png?resize=50,34 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 3200px) 100vw, 3200px\" \/>"caption-attachment-2318000\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Claravine’s data management platform.
Image Credits:<\/strong> Claravine<\/p><\/div><\/p>\nToward this end, Claravine provides a dashboard where companies can build taxonomies using descriptions, lists, values and referenceable fields. Using the platform, a user can bring in a tracking code dataset, for example, and standardize it — automatically verifying that no information is missing. Claravine also offers consulting services to assist companies with evaluating the current state of their data standards. For a fee, staffers outline alternative approaches, recording things like naming conventions, rules and custom attributes in a central location for reference.<\/p>"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n"font-weight: 400;\">“Data standards enable organizations to build a solid foundation of data by reducing human error upfront and unlocking a greater depth and breadth of data for use … By <\/span>"font-weight: 400;\">building in data integrity early on and pushing this data into core systems including cloud storage, you give back time to downstream teams otherwise lost to cleaning and translating,” Allen said.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\nAllen sees Claravine’s main competition as spreadsheet-based"font-weight: 400;\">processes, internally built worklows and — increasingly — no-code apps. While he admits it can be difficult to convince teams to manage their data standards in a platform as opposed to siloed solutions, he argues that the cost of not doing so is too high. <\/span><\/p>\n"font-weight: 400;\">Underlining Allen’s point, a recent Gartner"https:\/\/www.gartner.com\/en\/newsroom\/press-releases\/gartner-marketing-survey-finds-only-14--of-organizations-have-ac\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">survey<\/a> found that only 14% of companies have achieved what they consider to be a “360-degree view” of their customer, owing to poor-quality data and other organizational hurdles.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n"font-weight: 400;\">“While some organizations may try to define and distribute data requirements in documents, structured spreadsheets or homegrown solutions, these create immense challenges around change management, version control, access, and process resulting in challenges in the readiness and reliability of data, particularly for global organizations,” Allen said. “<\/span>"font-weight: 400;\">The status quo for marketing operations, measurement, and data teams is no longer good enough.”<\/span><\/p>\nMum’s the word on Claravine’s annual recurring revenue (ARR) — Allen declined to say — but the startup has close to 100 customers, including Under Armour, Ancestry and Vanguard. From 2020 to 2021,"font-weight: 400;\">Allen says that Claravine saw over 40% ARR growth and 95% gross revenue retention, which refers to the percentage of recurring revenue retained from existing customers, including cancellations.<\/span><\/p>\n"font-weight: 400;\">“Claravine has carved out a new category that continues to redefine how top brands manage their digital experience. We have been exceptionally impressed by Verl, his team, and their mission<\/span>"font-weight: 400;\">,” Stephanie Schneider, a partner at Five Elms Capital, told TechCrunch via email when contacted for comment. “Claravine is positioned to become a dominant player in the space as it continues to scale its platform and offerings. We are proud to support the company on this exciting growth trajectory.”<\/span><\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"Claravine, a self-described marketing data platform, today announced that it raised $16 million in a Series B round led by Five Elms Capital with participation from Grayhawk Capital, Next Frontier Capital, Peninsula Ventures, Kickstart Fund and Silverton Partners. CEO Verl Allen says that the new money, which brings the company’s total raised to $27.9 million, Partners","slug":"silverton-partners","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/50982769"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=50982769"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=50982769"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=50982769"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=50982769"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":449557042,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/startups\/","name":"Startups","slug":"startups","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/449557042"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=449557042"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=449557042"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=449557042"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=449557042"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2316367,"date":"2022-05-16T05:00:32","date_gmt":"2022-05-16T12:00:32","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2316367"},"modified":"2022-05-16T11:48:54","modified_gmt":"2022-05-16T18:48:54","slug":"akuity-raises-20m-to-simplify-kubernetes-container-management","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/16\/akuity-raises-20m-to-simplify-kubernetes-container-management\/","title":{"rendered":"Akuity raises $20M to simplify Kubernetes container management"},"content":{"rendered":""speakable-summary\">"http:\/\/akuity.io\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Akuity<\/a>, a provider of app delivery software for Kubernetes, today announced that it closed a $20 million Series A funding round led by Lead Edge Capital and Decibel Partners, bringing Akuity’s total raised to $25 million. Co-founder and CEO Hong Wang says that the funding will enable Akuity to expand the size of its workforce while contributing to the open source community.<\/p>\nApps are increasingly built using containers, or “microservices” packaged with all the necessary dependencies and configuration files. Kubernetes is open source software for deploying and managing these containers. While popular, managing containers with Kubernetes can become complex, particularly as legacy software moves to the cloud as a part of pandemic-prompted digital transformations.
"https:\/\/containerjournal.com\/topics\/container-management\/survey-sees-kubernetes-challenges-taking-a-toll\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">According<\/a> to one recent survey (albeit commissioned by a Kubernetes tooling vendor), over a third of developers and architects admit that Kubernetes has become a major source of burnout.<\/p>\nWang, Jesse Suen and Alexander Matyushentsev believed there must be an easier way. The three were founding engineers at Applatix, a Kubernetes management engine that was acquired by Intuit in 2018. A year earlier, Applatix had open sourced a project called Argo, a “container-native” workflow engine designed to streamline the process of specifying, scheduling and coordinating the running of apps on Kubernetes. While at Intuit following the Applatix acquisition, Wang, Suen and Matyushentsev investigated ways to foster Argo as oversight of the project was transferred to the Linux Foundation.<\/p>\n“Enterprises are well on their way toward containerization. However, as these organizations move to Kubernetes, they quickly discover that their existing, legacy tooling is ill-suited for delivering Kubernetes-native apps with its configuration-heavy design,” Suen told TechCrunch via email. “[W]hile Kubernetes is very powerful, it is extremely complex and provides a poor out-of-the-box developer experience. Because of this, organizations invest in platform and infrastructure teams, as well as developer experience teams, to standardize and ease their transition to Kubernetes. Building these teams is challenging, exacerbated by both high demand and low supply of Kubernetes expertise. Moreover, many of these organizations re-implementing the same patterns again and again and would benefit from a codified set of best practices and standardized tooling.”<\/p>\nSuen and Wang position Argo, and by extension Akuity, as a complement to the traditional continuous delivery (CD) solutions offered by vendors including"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/10\/13\/armory-scores-a-40m-series-c-to-continue-commercializing-open-source-spinnaker-project\/\">Armory<\/a>,"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2018\/06\/27\/cloudbees-raises-62m-for-its-devops-platform\/\">CloudBees<\/a> and"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/01\/14\/harness-snags-85m-series-c-on-1-7b-valuation-as-revenue-grows-3x\/\">Harness.io<\/a>. (In software development, “continuous delivery” refers to the engineering approach where teams create software in short cycles to ensure that it can be reliably released at any time.) Argo allows developers to create a “pipeline” for building apps and specify the pipeline as code, so that it can be built or upgraded using containers and run on other systems.<\/p>\n“Akuity was formed to help companies modernize their Kubernetes tooling, leveraging Argo, the leading open source suite of Kubernetes-native app delivery software,” Wang told TechCrunch in an email interview. “[With Akuity,] we are aiming to revolutionize the DevOps space and provide the most advanced toolset that empowers developers to get the maximum value out of Kubernetes.”<\/p>\nToward that end, Akuity is in the process of launching a fully managed version of Argo called Akuity Platform. Currently in closed beta ahead of general availability later this year, Akuity Platform adds features to Argo like deployment analytics and telemetry, health checks for app components and an audit trail and history of app events and API calls.<\/p>"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n“The number one problem we solve for enterprises is easing their transition to Kubernetes,” Matyushentsev, who recently became chief architect at Akuity, told TechCrunch via email. “With [Akuity,] businesses can enable a high frequency of deployment for quick delivery of new features and updates, decrease [the] lead time for changes and updates, … decrease mean time to recovery to recover quickly, … minimize change failure rate (i.e., the proportion of failures coming from changes), [and] increase the stability and reliability of apps and services.”<\/p>\nIt’s early days for Akuity, which has rivals in container-friendly CD tools like Flux CD and Jenkins X. But Wang pointed to Argo’s uptake as evidence that Akuity has the right approach. Production use of Argo increased by 115% year-over-year, according to a 2021"https:\/\/www.cncf.io\/reports\/cncf-annual-survey-2021\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">survey<\/a> by Cloud Native Computing Foundation, the Linux Foundation overseeing Argo. And since launching last October, Akuity has closed “several” deals with Fortune 1000 companies, Wang claims.<\/p>\nWhether that translates to strong momentum down the road remains to be seen — particularly without revenue numbers to go on. Regardless, it’s true that tooling and services built around Kubernetes represent a massive opportunity. A 2021 poll from Canonical"https:\/\/juju.is\/cloud-native-kubernetes-usage-report-2021\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">found<\/a> that 45.6% of organizations now use Kubernetes in production. A separate report estimates the market for Kubernetes solutions will reach $5.56 billion in 2028, up from $1.71 billion in 2021.<\/p>\n“Our product adoption accelerated during the pandemic,” Wang added. “Based on our conversations with customers, many of them are leveraging the Kubernetes adoption opportunities to refresh their developer tool stack. Argo becomes the default choice as it is Kubernetes-native and has the most vibrant open-source community in the CD space.”<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"Akuity, a provider of app delivery software for Kubernetes, today announced that it closed a $20 million Series A funding round led by Lead Edge Capital and Decibel Partners, bringing Akuity’s total raised to $25 million. Co-founder and CEO Hong Wang says that the funding will enable Akuity to expand the size of its workforce
