Edge Capital","slug":"lead-edge-capital","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576608081"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576608081"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576608081"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576608081"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576608081"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":449557042,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/startups\/","name":"Startups","slug":"startups","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/449557042"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=449557042"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=449557042"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=449557042"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=449557042"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2318341,"date":"2022-05-13T09:23:28","date_gmt":"2022-05-13T16:23:28","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2318341"},"modified":"2022-05-13T11:18:21","modified_gmt":"2022-05-13T18:18:21","slug":"inflection-ai-led-by-linkedin-and-deepmind-co-founders-raises-225m-to-transform-computer-human-interactions","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/13\/inflection-ai-led-by-linkedin-and-deepmind-co-founders-raises-225m-to-transform-computer-human-interactions\/","title":{"rendered":"Inflection AI, led by LinkedIn and DeepMind co-founders, raises $225M to transform computer-human interactions"},"content":{"rendered":""speakable-summary\">"https:\/\/inflection.ai\/\">Inflection AI<\/a>, the machine learning startup headed by LinkedIn co-founder Reid Hoffman and founding DeepMind member Mustafa Suleyman, has secured $225 million in equity financing,"https:\/\/www.sec.gov\/Archives\/edgar\/data\/1928505\/000108036822000029\/xslFormDX01\/primary_doc.xml\">according<\/a> to a filing with the U.S. Securities and Exchange Commission. The source of the capital isn’t yet clear — Inflection didn’t immediately respond to a request for more information — but the massive round suggests strong investor confidence in Suleyman, who serves as the company’s CEO.<\/p>\nPalo Alto, California-based Inflection has kept a low profile to date, granting relatively few interviews to the media. But in CNBC"https:\/\/www.cnbc.com\/2022\/01\/28\/mustafa-suleyman-deepmind-co-founder-quits-google-ai-role-to-be-vc.html\">profile<\/a> from January, Suleyman described wanting to build products that eliminate the need for people to simplify their ideas to communicate with machines, with the overarching goal being to leverage AI to help humans “talk” to computers.<\/p>\n“[Programming languages, mice, and other interfaces] are ways we simplify our ideas and reduce their complexity and in some ways their creativity and their uniqueness in order to get a machine to do something,” Suleyman told the publication. “It feels like we\u2019re on the cusp of being able to generate language to pretty much human-level performance. It opens up a whole new suite of things that we can do in the product space.”<\/p>\nThe concept of translating human intentions into a language computers can understand dates back decades. Even the best chatbots and voice assistants today haven\u2019t delivered on the promise, but Suleyman and Hoffman are betting that coming advancements in AI will make an intuitive human-computer interface possible within the next five years.<\/p>\nThey’ll have competition. Just last month,"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/04\/26\/2304039\/\">Adept<\/a>, a startup co-founded by former DeepMind, OpenAI and Google engineers and researchers, emerged from stealth with a similar concept: AI that can automate any software process. DeepMind itself has"https:\/\/arxiv.org\/pdf\/2202.08137.pdf\">explored<\/a> an approach for teaching AI to control computers, having an AI observe keyboard and mouse commands from people completing “instruction-following” computer tasks, such as booking a flight.<\/p>\nRegardless, the size of Inflection’s funding round reflects the high cost of building sophisticated AI systems. OpenAI is estimated to have spent millions of dollars developing GPT-3, the company’s system that can generate human-like text given a prompt.
"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/04\/29\/anthropics-quest-for-better-more-explainable-ai-attracts-580m\/\">Anthropic<\/a>, another startup developing cutting-edge AI models, recently raised over half a billion to — in co-founder Dario Amodei’s words — “explore the predictable scaling properties of machine learning systems.”<\/p>\nAI expertise doesn’t come cheap, either, particularly in the midst of a"https:\/\/fortune.com\/2022\/04\/26\/a-i-talent-shortage-recruiting\/\">talent shortage<\/a>. In 2018, a tax filing spotted by the New York Times"https:\/\/www.nytimes.com\/2018\/04\/19\/technology\/artificial-intelligence-salaries-openai.html\">revealed<\/a>\u00a0that OpenAI paid its top researcher, Ilya Sutskever, more than $1.9 million in 2016. Inflection recently poached AI experts from Google and Meta, CNBC"https:\/\/www.cnbc.com\/2022\/03\/29\/inflection-ai-reid-hoffmans-start-up-poaches-staff-from-google-meta.html\">reported<\/a> in March.<\/p>"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n\u201cEven at the bigger tech companies, there\u2019s a relatively small number of people actually building these [AI] models. One of the advantages of doing this in a startup is that we can go much faster and be more dynamic,\u201d Suleyman told CNBC. \u201cMy experience of building many, many teams over the last 15 years is that there is this golden moment when you really have a very close-knit, small, focused team. I\u2019m going to try and preserve that for as long as possible.\u201d<\/p>\nA cloud surrounds Inflection, somewhat, following"https:\/\/www.bloomberg.com\/news\/articles\/2019-08-21\/google-deepmind-co-founder-placed-on-leave-from-ai-lab\">reports<\/a> that Suleyman allegedly bullied staff members at Google, where he worked after being placed on administrative leave at DeepMind for controversy surrounding some of his projects. Google launched an investigation into his behavior at the time, according to the"https:\/\/www.wsj.com\/articles\/artificial-intelligence-will-define-googles-future-for-now-its-a-management-challenge-11611676945\">Wall Street Journal<\/a>, but it never made its findings public.<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"Inflection AI, the machine learning startup headed by LinkedIn co-founder Reid Hoffman and founding DeepMind member Mustafa Suleyman, has secured $225 million in equity financing, according to a filing with the U.S. Securities and Exchange Commission. The source of the capital isn’t yet clear — Inflection didn’t immediately respond to a request for more information D","slug":"form-d","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576615118"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576615118"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576615118"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576615118"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576615118"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":20250,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/funding\/","name":"funding","slug":"funding","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/20250"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=20250"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=20250"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=20250"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=20250"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":104406,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/inflection\/","name":"inflection","slug":"inflection","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/104406"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=104406"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=104406"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=104406"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=104406"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":40978,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/machine-learning\/","name":"machine learning","slug":"machine-learning","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/40978"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=40978"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=40978"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=40978"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=40978"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":449557042,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/startups\/","name":"Startups","slug":"startups","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/449557042"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=449557042"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=449557042"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=449557042"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=449557042"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2318076,"date":"2022-05-13T05:15:28","date_gmt":"2022-05-13T12:15:28","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2318076"},"modified":"2022-05-16T09:51:39","modified_gmt":"2022-05-16T16:51:39","slug":"deepminds-new-ai-can-perform-over-600-tasks-from-playing-games-to-controlling-robots","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/13\/deepminds-new-ai-can-perform-over-600-tasks-from-playing-games-to-controlling-robots\/","title":{"rendered":"DeepMind’s new AI can perform over 600 tasks, from playing games to controlling robots"},"content":{"rendered":""speakable-summary\">The ultimate achievement to some in the AI industry is creating a system with artificial general intelligence (AGI), or the ability to understand and learn any task that a human can. Long relegated to the domain of science fiction, it’s been suggested that AGI would bring about systems with the ability to reason, plan, learn, represent knowledge and communicate in natural language.<\/p>\nNot every expert is convinced that AGI is a realistic goal — or even possible. But it could be argued that DeepMind, the Alphabet-backed research lab, took a step toward it this week with the release of an AI system called"https:\/\/www.deepmind.com\/publications\/a-generalist-agent\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Gato<\/a>.<\/p>\nGato is what DeepMind describes as a “general-purpose” system, a system that can be taught to perform many different types of tasks. Researchers at DeepMind trained Gato to complete 604, to be exact, including captioning images, engaging in dialogue, stacking blocks with a real robot arm and playing Atari games.<\/p>\n“Most current AI systems work on a single task or narrow domain at a time. The significance of this work is mainly that one agent with one [model] can do hundreds of very different tasks, including to control a real robot and do basic captioning and chat,” Scott Reed, a researcher scientist at DeepMind and one of the co-creators of Gato, told TechCrunch via email.<\/p>\nJack Hessel, a research scientist at the Allen Institute for AI, points out that a single AI system that can solve many tasks isn’t new. For example, Google recently began using a system in Google Search called multitask unified model, or"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/09\/29\/google-introduces-a-new-way-to-search-that-combines-images-and-text-into-one-query\/\">MUM<\/a>, which can handle text, images and videos to perform tasks, from finding interlingual variations in the spelling of a word to relating a search query to an image. But whatis<\/em> potentially newer, here, Hessel says, is the diversity of the tasks that are tackled and the training method.<\/p>\n"attachment_2318161\" style=\"width: 690px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">"caption-attachment-2318161\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-large wp-image-2318161\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/627d13d743dc353a184da8d4_data_sequences.png?w=680\" alt=\"DeepMind Gato\" width=\"680\" height=\"495\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/627d13d743dc353a184da8d4_data_sequences.png 1299w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/627d13d743dc353a184da8d4_data_sequences.png?resize=150,109 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/627d13d743dc353a184da8d4_data_sequences.png?resize=300,218 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/627d13d743dc353a184da8d4_data_sequences.png?resize=768,559 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/627d13d743dc353a184da8d4_data_sequences.png?resize=680,495 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/627d13d743dc353a184da8d4_data_sequences.png?resize=50,36 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" \/>"caption-attachment-2318161\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">DeepMind’s Gato architecture.
Image Credits:<\/strong> DeepMind<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n“We’ve seen evidence previously that single models can handle surprisingly diverse sets of inputs,” Hessel told TechCrunch via email. “In my view, the core question when it comes to multitask learning … is whether the tasks complement each other or not. You could envision a more boring case if the model implicitly separates the tasks before solving them, e.g., ‘If I detect task A as an input, I will use subnetwork A. If I instead detect task B, I will use different subnetwork B.’ For that null hypothesis, similar performance could be attained by training A and B separately, which is underwhelming. In contrast, if training A and B jointly leads to improvements for either (or both!), then things are more exciting.”<\/p>"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\nLike all AI systems, Gato learned by example, ingesting billions of words, images from real-world and simulated environments, button presses, joint torques and more in the form of tokens. These tokens served to represent data in a way Gato could understand, enabling the system to — for example — tease out the mechanics of Breakout, or which combination of words in a sentence might make grammatical sense.<\/p>\nGato doesn’t necessarily do these taskswell<\/em>. For example, when chatting with a person, the system often responds with a superficial or factually incorrect reply (e.g. “Marseille” in response to “What is the capital of France?”). In captioning pictures, Gato misgenders people. And the system correctly stacks blocks using a real-world robot only 60% of the time.<\/p>\nBut on 450 of the 604 aforementioned tasks, DeepMind claims that Gato performs better than an expert more than half the time.<\/p>\n“If you’re of the mind that we need general [systems], which is a lot of folks in the AI and machine learning area, then [Gato is] a big deal,” Matthew Guzdial, an assistant professor of computing science at the University of Alberta, told TechCrunch via email. “I think people saying it’s a major step towards AGI are overhyping it somewhat, as we’re still not at human intelligence and likely not to get there soon (in my opinion). I’m personally more in the camp of many small models [and systems] being more useful, but there’s definitely benefits to these general models in terms of their performance on tasks outside their training data.”<\/p>\nCuriously, from an architectural standpoint, Gato isn’t dramatically different from many of the AI systems in production today. It shares characteristics in common with OpenAI’s GPT-3 in the sense that it’s a “Transformer.” Dating back to 2017, the Transformer has become the architecture of choice for complex reasoning tasks, demonstrating an aptitude for summarizing documents, generating music, classifying objects in images and analyzing protein sequences.<\/p>\n"attachment_2318162\" style=\"width: 690px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">"caption-attachment-2318162\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-large wp-image-2318162\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/ezgif-5-acebdcf906.gif?w=680\" alt=\"DeepMind Gato\" width=\"680\" height=\"680\" \/>"caption-attachment-2318162\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">The various tasks that Gato learned to complete.
Image Credits:<\/strong> DeepMind<\/p><\/div><\/p>\nPerhaps even more remarkably, Gato is orders of magnitude smaller than single-task systems, including GPT-3, in terms of the parameter count. Parameters are the parts of the system learned from training data and essentially define the skill of the system on a problem, such as generating text. Gato has just 1.2 billion, while GPT-3 has more than 170 billion.<\/p>\nDeepMind researchers kept Gato purposefully small so the system could control a robot arm in real time. But they hypothesize that — if scaled up — Gato could tackle any “task, behavior, and embodiment of interest.”<\/p>\nAssuming this turns out to be the case, several other hurdles would have to be overcome to make Gato superior in specific tasks to cutting-edge single-task systems, like Gato’s inability to learn continuously. Like most Transformer-based systems, Gato’s knowledge of the world is grounded in the training data and remains static. If you ask Gato a date-sensitive question, like the current president of the U.S., chances are it would respond incorrectly.<\/p>\nThe Transformer — and Gato, by extension — has another limitation in its context window, or the amount of information the system can “remember” in the context of a given task. Even the best Transformer-based language models can’t write a lengthy essay, much less a book, without failing to remember key details and thus losing track of the plot. The forgetting happens in any task, whether writing or controlling a robot, which is why some experts have"https:\/\/venturebeat.com\/2021\/04\/09\/ai-weekly-continual-learning-offers-a-path-toward-more-humanlike-ai\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">called<\/a> it the “Achilles’ heel” of machine learning.<\/p>\nFor these reasons and others, Mike Cook, a member of the Knives & Paintbrushes research collective, cautions against assuming Gato is a path to truly general-purpose AI.<\/p>\n“I think the result is open to misinterpretation, somewhat. It sounds exciting that the AI is able to do all of these tasks that sound very different, because to us it sounds like writing text is very different to controlling a robot. But in reality this isn’t all too different from GPT-3 understanding the difference between ordinary English text and Python code,” Cook told TechCrunch via email. “Gato receives specific training data about these tasks, just like any other AI of its type, and it learns how patterns in the data relate to one another, including learning to associate certain kinds of inputs with certain kinds of outputs. This isn’t to say this is easy, but to the outside observer this might sound like the AI can also make a cup of tea or easily learn another ten or fifty other tasks, and it can’t do that. We know that current approaches to large-scale modelling can let it learn multiple tasks at once. I think it’s a nice bit of work, but it doesn’t strike me as a major stepping stone on the path to anything.”<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"The ultimate achievement to some in the AI industry is creating a system with artificial general intelligence (AGI), or the ability to understand and learn any task that a human can. learning","slug":"machine-learning","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/40978"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=40978"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=40978"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=40978"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=40978"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":668,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/research\/","name":"research","slug":"research","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/668"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=668"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=668"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=668"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=668"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":13426,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/robotics\/","name":"robotics","slug":"robotics","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/13426"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=13426"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=13426"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=13426"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=13426"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2313897,"date":"2022-05-12T11:00:29","date_gmt":"2022-05-12T18:00:29","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2313897"},"modified":"2022-05-12T11:39:11","modified_gmt":"2022-05-12T18:39:11","slug":"tidio-raises-25m-to-automate-customer-service-interactions","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/12\/tidio-raises-25m-to-automate-customer-service-interactions\/","title":{"rendered":"Tidio raises $25M to automate customer service interactions"},"content":{"rendered":""speakable-summary\">During the pandemic especially, it’s become overwhelming for small- and medium-sized businesses (SMBs) to answer all of their customer service requests. A Freshworks"https:\/\/www.freshworks.com\/assets\/resources\/The-New-CX-Mandate-US-Report.pdf?tactic_id=4098694&utm_source=Email&utm_medium=SM-CX&utm_campaign=New-CX-Mandate-US\">survey<\/a> found that companies experienced a 71% increase in overall contact volume between February 2020 and January 2021, and expect it to increase further. At the same time, customers — while empathetic — have become more demanding. The same poll shows that 68% of customer service managers have seen an increase in customer expectations.<\/p>\nWhat’s a company to do? Automation is one route to more manageable customer experience workloads, potentially. Enter Tidio, a platform that aims to become a one-stop shop for companies corresponding with customers across different channels (e.g., email and SMS). Leveraging a combination of live chat apps and AI-powered chatbots, as well as analytics, Tidio attempts to scale customer service operations even at small companies without the benefit of dedicated staff.<\/p>\nCustomer service automation platforms like Tidio aren’t exactly cutting edge. To name a few, there’s"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/12\/03\/ultimate-ai-scores-20m-for-a-supportive-approach-to-customer-service-automation\/\">Ultimate.ai<\/a>, a data-ingesting, bot-builder platform and"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/11\/05\/ushur-raises-25m-for-its-no-code-platform-to-build-customer-communication-flows\/\">Ushur<\/a>, which offers a service for businesses to create AI-based communication flows. Ada also slots into the category — it features chatbots powered by a natural language processing engine.<\/p>\nWhat makes Tidio stand out, co-founder and CEO Tytus Go\u0142as asserts, is its simplicity in terms of implementation and structure. Tidio integrates with third-party services including email providers, Facebook, Instagram, WordPress and Shopify, allowing teams to manage customer interactions from a shared inbox. Plans range from free for two users to $332.50 per month (billed annually) for unlimited users and other extras.<\/p>\n"attachment_2313990\" style=\"width: 1010px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">"caption-attachment-2313990\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2313990\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/12102e2b69f289090c453e43ce31d18a.gif\" alt=\"Tidio\" width=\"1000\" height=\"514\" \/>"caption-attachment-2313990\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Creating a conversation flow using Tidio’s visual dashboard.
Image Credits:<\/strong> Tidio<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n“Most of our clients get"il\">Tidio<\/span> up and running within minutes and are seeing the value of our product within the same day. Our impact is twofold — you can streamline communication and increase your sales with our chatbot functionality,” Go\u0142as told TechCrunch in an email interview. “[O]ur chatbots and sales generation features have a direct impact on return on investment and help increase sales and revenue — sometimes covering the entire cost of the Tidio subscription in one day.”<\/p>\nTidio is the brainchild of Go\u0142as and Marcin Wiktor, who co-founded the company in 2013. What started as a digital advertising agency targeted at SMBs evolved into a development house for online marketing tools, one of which was Tidio. After the tool gained traction, Go\u0142as and Wiktor decided to pivot and make it their focus.<\/p>"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\nInvestors endorsed the move. Today, Tidio announced that it raised $25 million in a Series B round led by PeakSpan Capital with participation from Inovo Venture Partners and InPost CEO Rafa\u0142 Brzoska, bringing Tidio’s total raised to $26.8 million,<\/p>\nTidio provides a list of visitors on a company’s website, which owners can use to interact with them in various ways — either in real time (via chat) or automatically (via chatbot). For example, the platform can be programmed to send a “Welcome back” message to a return customer along with a unique discount code. Tidio also captures information like the source of web traffic, the amount of time customers spend on particular webpages and which products are viewed most often.<\/p>\n"ltr\">“We are using our custom dataset and state-of-the-art models to improve the language understanding capabilities of our models,” Go\u0142as said. “[One of these models] automatically detects any question topics in each new chat conversation. The platform then groups the topics by popularity, with the system recommending a user configure their [chatbot] to automate answers to the most common customers’ questions, such as those pertaining to order status, shipping status and returns.”<\/p>\n"ltr\">This type of automation — assuming it works as advertised — can save businesses time on repetitive tasks, Go\u0142as argues, allowing them to focus on building customer relationships. Of course, not all customers"https:\/\/www.egain.com\/is-chatbot-customer-service-effective-customers-say-yes\/\">prefer to speak with chatbots<\/a>, and privacy-forward browsers might obfuscate the customer data Tidio collects for personalization. But the startup’s sales pitch seemingly won over the more than 23,000 businesses that currently pay for Tidio, which used the platform to automate over 86,000 conversations in the last month alone.<\/p>\n"ltr\">Go\u0142as says that Tidio has been cash-flow positive and seen 7.7x revenue growth for the last three years — further highlighting the demand. The company claims that its platform is used by more than 510 million unique users and 3% of the merchants on Shopify.<\/p>\n“Customer experience is very often connected with how businesses are communicating with customers and they can see excellent results by showing that they care and understand their customers’ problems,” Go\u0142as said. “With that in mind, it’s imperative that"il\">Tidio<\/span> give store owners the space and time to have those meaningful conversations.”<\/p>\nTidio plans to put the new capital toward marketing and expanding its 140-person workforce. The company aims to hire 100 people in the next year.<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"During the pandemic especially, it’s become overwhelming for small- and medium-sized businesses (SMBs) to answer all of their customer service requests. At the same time, customers — while empathetic aims to supercharge chats with async video messaging"},"content":{"rendered":""speakable-summary\">"https:\/\/www.usebubbles.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Bubbles<\/a>, a startup that pitches its platform as the “anti-Zoom” for video messaging, today announced that it closed an $8.5 million funding round led by"font-weight: 400;\">Khosla Ventures, Craft Ventures, Streamlined Ventures, 468 Ventures and Bain Capital. Co-founder and CEO Tom Medema said the money will be used to further develop Bubbles’ platform while ramping up the company’s customer acquisition efforts.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n"font-weight: 400;\">Bubbles adds threaded video, audio and text comments to workers’ desktops — an idea that Medema said came to him when he was the CTO at Bloomon, a flower delivery service in the Netherlands. There, Medema managed a distributed team that relied on what’s become the <\/span>"font-weight: 400;\">typical software stack for workplace collaboration: Slack, Zoom and Google Docs.<\/span><\/p>\n"font-weight: 400;\">“<\/span>"font-weight: 400;\">As the team grew, and collaboration became ever more crucial, I quickly realized this collection of tools fell short — and our team paid the price. It was a maddening game of calendar tetris, constant notifications, and continuous undoing of miscommunications,” Medema told TechCrunch via email. “<\/span>"font-weight: 400;\">What I realized was that our so-called productivity tools were actually throttling our productivity. We are ‘always on,’ but failing to accomplish real work. Searching for a solution, hacking my way into our outdated systems and processes, I came up with the vision for Bubbles.”<\/span><\/p>\n"font-weight: 400;\">Medema began work on Bubbles in 2019, but he argues that the tool has become even more relevant with the normalization of work-from-home setups. Medema, a pessimist when it comes to remote work — or, more accurately, typical remote work software — points to a<\/span>"font-weight: 400;\">\u00a0<\/span>"https:\/\/www.microsoft.com\/en-us\/worklab\/work-trend-index\/hybrid-work\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">"font-weight: 400;\">2021 study <\/span><\/a>"font-weight: 400;\">of Microsoft and LinkedIn employees that found that employees are burned out and “digitally exhausted.”<\/span><\/p>\n"attachment_2310106\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">"caption-attachment-2310106\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2310106\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/04\/822f21b5-1506-4ab2-a638-b26c73dce689.jpg\" alt=\"Bubbles\" width=\"1024\" height=\"640\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/04\/822f21b5-1506-4ab2-a638-b26c73dce689.jpg 2432w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/04\/822f21b5-1506-4ab2-a638-b26c73dce689.jpg?resize=150,94 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/04\/822f21b5-1506-4ab2-a638-b26c73dce689.jpg?resize=300,188 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/04\/822f21b5-1506-4ab2-a638-b26c73dce689.jpg?resize=768,480 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/04\/822f21b5-1506-4ab2-a638-b26c73dce689.jpg?resize=680,425 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/04\/822f21b5-1506-4ab2-a638-b26c73dce689.jpg?resize=1536,960 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/04\/822f21b5-1506-4ab2-a638-b26c73dce689.jpg?resize=2048,1280 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/04\/822f21b5-1506-4ab2-a638-b26c73dce689.jpg?resize=50,31 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/>"caption-attachment-2310106\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Image Credits:<\/strong> Bubbles<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n"font-weight: 400;\">“Our mission is to return joy to work: to get back to creativity and productivity, to foster deep work, and to mitigate burnout by moving away from hyper-responsiveness and real-time communication towards greater asynchronous communication,” Medema continued. “Async platforms are at the top of their list as it frees up employees\u2019 time to do deep work, and mitigates the digital burnout that occurs by being overwhelmed with meetings and notifications all day.”<\/span><\/p>\nWith Bubbles, users can asynchronously send"font-weight: 400;\"> and receive messages — video or otherwise — with threading, which Medema claims allows for more thoughtful feedback. Historically, the challenge with asynchronous video tools has been user buy-in. It’s easier to fire off a quick Slack message than record and edit a video, after all. But Bubbles attempts to make the process less unappealing by streamlining many aspects of it, dispensing with passwords, onboarding steps and even usernames.<\/span><\/p>"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n"font-weight: 400;\">Users start a Bubbles conversation from a web browser, capturing their perspective through video, audio or a screen recording and inviting collaborators. This begins a threaded conversation where participants can comment at and add reactions to specific time codes.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\nFuture plans include improved discovery, specifically semantic search and topic modeling, which"font-weight: 400;\">Medema says will allow Bubbles users to “intuitively search across conversations.” Beyond this, Medema says that Bubbles will introduce transcription and summarization capabilities, automatically highlighting important sections in videos and suggesting action items.<\/span><\/p>\n“‘Quick questions’ on Slack, inboxes full of emails, and a never-ending stream of notifications hold us back from achieving the precious state of deep work and flow,”"font-weight: 400;\"> Medema said. “Bubbles is an <\/span>"font-weight: 400;\">async-first<\/span>"font-weight: 400;\"> tool, designed to work outside of the outdated construct of the meeting — allowing users to collaborate on work at every individual\u2019s optimal time.”<\/span><\/p>\nBubbles isn’t the first to attempt the asynchronous messaging paradigm. Others include"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/04\/asynchronous-video-startup-weet-just-launched-to-cement-bonds-and-know-how-within-companies\/\">Weet<\/a>,"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2019\/02\/27\/threads-emerges-from-stealth-with-10-5m-from-sequoia-for-a-new-take-on-enabaling-work-conversations\/\">Threads<\/a> and"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/06\/14\/could-claap-an-asynchronous-video-meetings-platform-end-the-tyranny-of-zoom-calls\/\">Claap<\/a>. Slack"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/09\/21\/slack-releases-clips-video-tool-announces-16-salesforce-integrations\/\">recently<\/a> dipped a toe with Slack Clips, which lets users embed audio, video and screen recordings within channels and direct messages.<\/p>\n"font-weight: 400;\">Medema claims that Bubbles recently surpassed 20,000 monthly active users — a healthy number, to be sure — but the trick will be commercializing it. Bubbles is currently free. Monetization plans include a team tier with folders and granular access control.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n"attachment_2310105\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">"caption-attachment-2310105\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2310105\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/04\/ba707358-5be8-4e33-8df3-a573ed853b0e.jpg\" alt=\"Bubbles\" width=\"1024\" height=\"640\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/04\/ba707358-5be8-4e33-8df3-a573ed853b0e.jpg 2432w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/04\/ba707358-5be8-4e33-8df3-a573ed853b0e.jpg?resize=150,94 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/04\/ba707358-5be8-4e33-8df3-a573ed853b0e.jpg?resize=300,188 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/04\/ba707358-5be8-4e33-8df3-a573ed853b0e.jpg?resize=768,480 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/04\/ba707358-5be8-4e33-8df3-a573ed853b0e.jpg?resize=680,425 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/04\/ba707358-5be8-4e33-8df3-a573ed853b0e.jpg?resize=1536,960 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/04\/ba707358-5be8-4e33-8df3-a573ed853b0e.jpg?resize=2048,1280 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/04\/ba707358-5be8-4e33-8df3-a573ed853b0e.jpg?resize=50,31 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/>"caption-attachment-2310105\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Image Credits:<\/strong> Bubbles<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n"font-weight: 400;\">“The past two years have taught leaders not only that work was more than capable of being completed from home, but also highlighted that employees work better with flexibility and control of their own schedules. However, by hyper-accelerating our conversion to remote work, it also exposed the deep flaws in our existing remote work tools, which were not really designed to be used in a remote world,” Medema said. “<\/span>"font-weight: 400;\">Bubbles\u2019 async nature [keeps] a record of conversations as they happen. This also helps partially overcome the knowledge loss that occurs due to employee turnover, which is a key challenge in today\u2019s work environment.”<\/span><\/p>\nBubbles has eight employees. The company plans to double the size of the team by the end of the year.<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"Bubbles, a startup that pitches its platform as the “anti-Zoom” for video messaging, today announced that it closed an $8.5 million funding round led by Khosla Ventures, Craft Ventures, Streamlined Ventures, 468 Ventures and Bain Capital. json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=20250"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=20250"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=20250"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2313590,"date":"2022-05-12T05:00:28","date_gmt":"2022-05-12T12:00:28","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2313590"},"modified":"2022-05-12T10:21:41","modified_gmt":"2022-05-12T17:21:41","slug":"2313590","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/12\/2313590\/","title":{"rendered":"Customer service automation startup Lang lands $15M"},"content":{"rendered":""speakable-summary\">The customer experience is one of the most important focus areas for businesses.
"https:\/\/www.pwc.com\/us\/en\/services\/consulting\/library\/consumer-intelligence-series\/future-of-customer-experience.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">According<\/a> to PwC, among all customers, 73% point to experience as an important factor in their purchasing decisions, behind price and product quality. But the pandemic increased the workload of support teams, making it more difficult to hire customer service agents and keep the attrition low while maintaining a high bar for customer experience. The"https:\/\/hbr.org\/sponsored\/2021\/08\/heres-what-happens-when-you-focus-on-employees-to-better-serve-your-customers#:~:text=The%20average%20customer%2Dservice%20representative,average%20turnover%20in%20other%20departments.\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">average<\/a> contact center turnover rate is as high as 45% — at least twice that of other departments.<\/p>\nThere is no silver bullet. But Jorge Penalva is a strong proponent of using automation technologies to help bridge the gaps in customer service. He would be — he’s the co-founder of"http:\/\/lang.ai\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Lang.ai<\/a>, a startup developing a platform that automatically tags customer conversations to resolve service issues ostensibly more quickly. By applying intelligence to service interactions, Penalva asserts that technology like Lang’s can surface valuable insights to guide product experiences and strategies.<\/p>\n"font-weight: 400;\">“Automation in customer support is not new. As companies grow larger, a common approach is deploying automation via self-service chatbots to grow more efficiently and deflect customer inquiries. Ultimately, the goal of Lang is to be a core layer of the customer experience stack that enables teams to build automations and extract better insights by structuring qualitative data,” Penalva told TechCrunch in an email interview.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\nLang, which today announced that it raised $10.5 million in a Series A funding round led by"font-weight: 400;\">Nava Ventures (bringing its total raised to $15 million), uses AI to extract concepts from customer requests in existing help desk platforms like Zendesk and Intercom. The no-code product appends incoming messages, including emails and texts, with labels like “Talk to agent,” “Delivery issue” and “Platform question.” Using Lang, companies can visually group concepts identified in customer support data and set up automations that trigger with specific labels (e.g. respond to questions about package deliveries with boilerplate text).<\/span><\/p>\n"attachment_2317547\" style=\"width: 593px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">"caption-attachment-2317547\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-large wp-image-2317547\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/60f83409a5294bd1516ead0d_tags-banking-services-accounts-credit-cardx2.png?w=583\" alt=\"Lang.ai\" width=\"583\" height=\"680\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/60f83409a5294bd1516ead0d_tags-banking-services-accounts-credit-cardx2.png 956w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/60f83409a5294bd1516ead0d_tags-banking-services-accounts-credit-cardx2.png?resize=128,150 128w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/60f83409a5294bd1516ead0d_tags-banking-services-accounts-credit-cardx2.png?resize=257,300 257w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/60f83409a5294bd1516ead0d_tags-banking-services-accounts-credit-cardx2.png?resize=768,897 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/60f83409a5294bd1516ead0d_tags-banking-services-accounts-credit-cardx2.png?resize=583,680 583w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/60f83409a5294bd1516ead0d_tags-banking-services-accounts-credit-cardx2.png?resize=43,50 43w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 583px) 100vw, 583px\" \/>"caption-attachment-2317547\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Image Credits:<\/strong> Lang.ai<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n"font-weight: 400;\">Penalva said that he and his co-founders, Borja Gonz\u00e1lez and Enrique Fueyo Ram\u00edrez, came up with the idea for Lang while working together at a previous startup,"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2015\/03\/18\/sentisis-series-a\/\">Sentisis<\/a>, a natural language processing platform for Spanish. There, Penalva said they saw business teams were unable to leverage customer service data without the expertise of their data science departments, which had higher-priority work on their plates.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n"font-weight: 400;\">“We realized that we had to think about the problem in a completely different way, not by applying current AI models (built for, and by, engineers) and simplifying them for business users, but instead by creating a no-code platform intended, from its inception, for business users,” Penalva said. “<\/span>"font-weight: 400;\">It\u2019s not just the technology or just the user experience. Both are equally important and that was our ‘aha!’ moment.”<\/span><\/p>"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\nLang isn’t alone in using AI to auto-tag customer service messages. Platforms like Levity.ai and Chatdesk also auto-label incoming service requests, including emails and texts. But"font-weight: 400;\">Penalva believes that Lang is differentiated both by its technology and go-to-market approach. For example, he said, Lang uses AI systems tailored for particular customers’ domains (e.g. retail, food services, healthcare) to recognize industry jargon and adapt to changes like emerging customer support issues. The startup partners with<\/span>"font-weight: 400;\"> vendors developing frontend and backend customer service automation products, such as business intelligence tools, to sell Lang as a complementary offering.<\/span><\/p>\n"font-weight: 400;\">“In making unstructured data usable by tagging it, Lang becomes a data platform that can be leveraged for automations, chatbot workflows and machine learning. <\/span>"font-weight: 400;\">[Moreover, the platform] becomes the system of record for all insights across unstructured customer experience data, providing a centralized source for insights across disparate sources,” Penalva said. <\/span>"font-weight: 400;\">“To date, our biggest competition for budget share has not been other platforms but rather displacing the status quo: the hiring or outsourcing of more customer experience agents.”<\/span><\/p>\nIt’s early days for Lang, but the company counts"font-weight: 400;\">Stitch Fix, Ramp, Hippo Insurance and Freshly among its customers. Annual recurring revenue — Penalva declined to reveal — grew 11x in the last five quarters preceding the Series A.<\/span><\/p>\nWith the proceeds from the latest round (which also saw participation from"font-weight: 400;\">Oceans Ventures, Forum and Flexport Fund)<\/span>, Penalva said that 25-employee Lang will invest in R&D and its go-to-market teams. On the subject of the former, Penalva says that Lang will work to identify ways to connect support conversations to purchase data to determine, for example, how likely someone with a certain issue will continue purchasing a product. Future versions of the Lang platform will make automation recommendations for customer service teams based on the actions agents commonly perform.<\/p>\n“"font-weight: 400;\">We believe data is the most valuable asset for support and customer experience teams,” Penalva said. “By structuring data in a simple and reliable way across all of their customer interactions, our mission is to help support teams gain their seat at the leadership table, so that support is no longer viewed as a cost center but as a revenue driver.”<\/span><\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"The customer experience is one of the most important focus areas for businesses. According to PwC, among all customers, 73% point to experience as an important factor in their purchasing decisions, behind price and product quality. But the pandemic increased the workload of support teams, making it more difficult to hire customer service agents and debuts Cloud Run jobs for containerized, scripted tasks"},"content":{"rendered":""speakable-summary\">During a developer keynote at Google I\/O 2022, Google unveiled"https:\/\/codelabs.developers.google.com\/codelabs\/codelabs\/cloud-run-jobs?hl=en#0\">Cloud Run jobs<\/a>, an extension of Google Cloud’s service for developing and deploying containerized apps using languages including Go, Python and Java. Cloud Run jobs are designed for containers that run to completion and don’t serve requests, such as data processing and administrative jobs, and when multiple copies of a container must run in parallel.<\/p>\nCloud Run launched in 2019, adding to Google Cloud’s then-rapidly-growing serverless compute stack. As the demand for serverless"https:\/\/www.oreilly.com\/radar\/oreilly-serverless-survey-2019-concerns-what-works-and-what-to-expect\/\">climbs<\/a>, it would appear that expansions like Cloud Run jobs are an attempt to beat back against rivals like Azure and Amazon Web Services.<\/p>\nAvailable in preview starting today, Cloud Run jobs can be used to run a script to perform database migrations or other operational tasks, like sending invoices every month. Relative to other platforms that support long-running jobs, Cloud Run jobs start quickly after creation, Google claims, with simple containers starting in as little as 10 seconds.<\/p>\nTo use Cloud Run jobs, developers create a job, which encapsulates all the configuration needed to run the job including the container image, region, environment variables. Then, they set up the job to run on a schedule or manually run the job, creating a new execution of the job.<\/p>\nDuring the preview, Cloud Run jobs supports up to 50 executions from the same or different jobs concurrently per project per region. Users can view existing jobs, start executions and monitor execution status from Cloud Console’s Cloud Run Jobs page; Cloud Console doesn’t currently support creating new jobs.<\/p>\nCloud Run jobs arrives alongside an updated"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/11\/google-updates-its-firebase-backend-as-a-service-to-make-app-development-faster\/\">Firebase<\/a>, Google’s popular back-end-as-a-service platform, and"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/11\/google-cloud-launches-alloydb-a-new-fully-managed-postgresql-database-service\/\">AlloyDB<\/a>, a new fully managed PostgreSQL database service. Arguably the more interesting of the two, AlloyDB features — as my colleague Frederic Lardinois writes — a custom machine learning-based caching service to learn a customer\u2019s access patterns and then convert Postgres\u2019 row format into an in-memory columnar format that can be analyzed significantly faster.<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"During a developer keynote at Google I\/O 2022, Google unveiled Cloud Run jobs, an extension of Google Cloud’s service for developing and deploying containerized apps using languages including Go, Python and Java. Cloud Run jobs are designed for containers that run to completion and don’t serve requests, such as data processing and administrative jobs, and
